### Post by siamesekatz on 2009-08-23
Hi All

I have an old -3rd hand-  T21 800mz P3 325mb RAM 80GB HDD etc.
This PC really rocks. I have a dual boot Wubi 9.04 and XP PRO (very fast and stable too). I use it for every thing DTP, Surfing, DVDs and office. I have burned well over 300 CDs on the CDR/DVD drive and it's still good to go.

I started with Hardy then upgraded to Interpid then finally fresh Jaunty install - all are Xubuntu.
Had a few probs with each. Hardy seemed to work completely "out of the box" but after updating it killed the X. I later found that one has to add a string to the xorg conf file setting the Savage card to PCI . The upgrade to Intrepid did the same thing in breaking the X...
The other problem was that while updating intrepid it corupted the nic driver, one minute it was working then suddenly no eth0 only lo0 :-( .I had to remove the eepro module and add the older eepro100 module. 
Jaunty had the same problem with the nic (but from the start no eth0) I did the same adding of the eepro module and it worked the trick!
Jaunty's X is much better and faster too, I can now even enable compositing with out the lags in display :-) Also jaunty boots way faster than 8.04 and 8.1

This T21 is really a miracle I must say. I've had it for 6 years living in india and it is still rocking! If any PC can last in India for more than a couple of years its truly amazing. 

I also have a HP nx6325 (1.8gz Truirno x2 1gbRam etc) but it cant realy handle the invironment (monsoon and all) or power aswell as the T21. The screen is dying (new lines of blue, yello and cyan each day 7 in total:() and on the whole not in as good conditition as the T21 which is much older and has zero marks or dead pixels. I know that thinkpads are the best, and i tried to convince the my dad to get me one(T61) but in the end we could get the HP from his work real cheap. Its kinda cool but I fear it wont last long

So this brings me to the nest part of this post: I now hope to get a replacemnt thinkpad for the HP. Basicly Its a R500 or a SL500

Can anybody tell me how the SL500 is compared to the R500, do you think it will last as long? Can it handle hectic heat, cold, humidity, bus rides?  Or should I just go with the R500 and save myself the headache. Both seem to be quite cheap at the moment so it seems that either are in my range :-)

What do you think R or the SL?

### Post by rootless on 2009-08-24
I love rustbucket very much. (Rustbucket is my six year old R40 that I bought for $180.)

I think that Thinkpad users will understand why I have named my laptop. Over the years, I've put her through hell and back, ripped out and replaced components, dropped her, coaxed parts to fit back into place, gotten her a little bit soggy, left her in a hundred degree car all day, and once accidentally froze her in my backpack while walking one cold January night. (oops) 

During this time, I have crafted all of my software from source, compiled kernels, spoken directly to the cards and the kernel, scripted and tweaked and patched modded out everything beyond recognition, and seen every cryptic error message in *nix history, and I believe she has developed a distinct personality.

The old rustbucket. Always keeps chugging along. Never overheats. Gets the job done, even if I need to give her screen a little coaxing to get it to stop fuzzing. (maybe this is a driver problem?) This old box has never let me down, and when she dies, I don't know what I'll do. I hope that some of her parts will end up giving me a few more years in a new box.

Here's to the Thinkpad. I believe that Thinkpads are about as close as you can come to expressing the *nix philosophy in copper and silicon.

### Post by SaintDanBert on 2009-09-12
**Emperor Linux "Raven" Tablet (Lenovo Thinkpad X61 Tablet)**

I'm running dual-boot Win-XP Pro Tablet Edition and Ubuntu Hardy (v8.04 LTS) with few real complaints. Business friends see the Thinkpad and think business. They then see Ubuntu and think "Huh?!" ... "Wow!!" 

There is a list of wants for better and different. Most notably, 3D desktop effects (Compiz) does not play well with "tablet".  "Tablet mode" means the screen is in portrait orientation and you use a stylus instead of a mouse and keyboard.

Emperor Linux is terrific as a vendor. They would benefit from a better presence online. Real humans answer the phone and they have real answers to my questions.

Cheers,
~~~ 0;-Dan

### Post by fsando on 2009-11-08
> **matt221171 said:**
>  <snip> I am using Vista pro if this makes any difference
Hope someone can help and appreciate any time given to this issue,many thanks Matt.

Do you mean you're not using Ubuntu? If that's the case you may be somewhat off track in this forum. If you are in fact using some version of Ubuntu my guess is you are using Karmic (Ubuntu 9.10). Personally I would suggest you use either version 9.04 (Jaunty) or the one before (Intrepid 8.10). There are two reasons for this: 

1) A brand spanking new version of any OS is bound to show problems of various kinds so if you're a new user you will not know if the problems you're experiencing are due to your lack of knowledge or due to bugs in the os. 

2) From the reports around the Net I get the impression that Karmic specifically is actually a pre-release for the upcoming Ubuntu 10.04 next year which means there are probably more problems in Karmic than would normally be expected.

My personal experience with a Lenovo T500 is that Ubuntu 8.10 works the best (or perhaps even 8.04). 

Ubuntu 9.04 is known to have a lot of problems with intel graphics (I believe your x200 has intel graphics only). 

Both 9.04 and 9.10 have a lot of problems with sound. There is a shift going on in the linux world from one type of sound system to another - this appears to take quite some time (a hen vs. egg problem) sound drivers and sound applications support one or the other so when distributions make changes they are bound to break something until everybody follows the same standard which is not easy. This shift has been under way at least for a year and now some distributions are starting to push harder (like ubuntu) trying to force a modernization of sound in Linux.

---

### Post by Miguel on 2009-12-03
> **Astinsan said:**
> 
I do realize that KMS is pretty much beta for ati (alpha for intel). 


I don't know about your other issues, but KMS is actually best with Intel. Intel + KMS is between beta and RC, while KMS for ATI is experimental. 

It would appear, however, that your Radeon 7500 doesn't have any power management when you're using KMS. I'd file a bug and, if you still have Karmic installed, have a go at xorg-edgers PPA.

### Post by n.l.o on 2010-05-26
Do not know where to put this.

I changed the icons for the gnome panel applet, just inverted the colors more or less. Looks better in Lucid. After installing it just put the new icons in: /usr/share/pixmaps/gnome-hdaps-applet/

(hdaps-paused.png is just the image that is shown in the "add panel applet" list)

PS.
To install the hdaps gnome panel applet type these lines into the terminal (this is not the hdaps kernel module it self, just the panel applet):
```

sudo apt-get install libpanel-applet2-dev
mkdir gnome-hdaps
cd gnome-hdaps
wget http://www.zen24593.zen.co.uk/hdaps/gnome-hdaps-applet-20081204.tar.gz
tar xfvz gnome-hdaps-applet-20081204.tar.gz
sudo gcc $(pkg-config --cflags --libs libpanelapplet-2.0) -o gnome-hdaps-applet gnome-hdaps-applet.c
sudo cp gnome-hdaps-applet /usr/bin/
sudo mkdir /usr/share/pixmaps/gnome-hdaps-applet/
sudo cp *.png /usr/share/pixmaps/gnome-hdaps-applet/
sudo cp GNOME_HDAPS_StatusApplet.server /usr/lib/bonobo/servers/
cd ..
rm -R gnome-hdaps

```

Sharing is caring

 Timing cached reads:   3274 MB in  2.00 seconds = 1638.75 MB/sec

### Post by Miguel on 2010-06-23
Those figures seem to be around right. There has to be something else. But because it's a new HD and you formatted it in order to install ubuntu, I doubt it would be excessive fragmentation. Are you using LVM or encryption or something fancy?

---

### Post by fsando on 2010-06-23
I don't use encryption, I don't know if I use LVM (don't know what it is really)

---

### Post by Miguel on 2010-06-23
> **fsando said:**
> I don't use encryption, I don't know if I use LVM (don't know what it is really)

LVM stands for "Logical Volume Manager". It is a nifty way of forgetting about partitions and stop worrying about their sizes, but it comes with a penalty hit. I think only the alternate and the server installers allow you to use LVM in an install. 

As an example of the penalty hit, my workstation (A Dell with Red Hat 5.5) with LVM took about 5 times as long to "./configure" openMPI compared to a scratch physical partition.

But I fear that if it's not any of these things and if you don't have fancy flags in /etc/fstab I'm not knowledgeable enough to troubleshoot your HD. Sorry.

---

### Post by fsando on 2010-06-23
Thanks for your replies.

In that case I'm not using LVM but there may well be a fancy flag (or a missing flag) in my fstab. 

My setup is actually a litte special. I have lots of partitions all 4 primary one of which is extended and filled up with further partitions. I have 8.10, 9.10 and 10.04 installed along each other. Have been meaning to clean up the whole thing - but haven't really had the time yet.

I have two data partitions mounted as ~/data1 and ~/data2 and my webroot mounted as a seperate partition at /var/www. The point of this setup is that every new install gets the same old data partitions and the webroot. The largest data partition (250Gb) is mounted as second to last with the swap as the last. This may be a reason for delays - they (I believe) only really occur with the large data partition.

---

### Post by shuttleworthwannabe on 2010-06-26
> **MikeDK said:**
> another thing you could do is, install tpfand from launchpad, to control your fan on the thinkpad.
[https://launchpad.net/~tp-fan/+archive/ppa](https://launchpad.net/~tp-fan/+archive/ppa)

just use the jaunty archives, it works fine in lucid

You know I have tried installing tpfand, but not sure how to configure this??

anyway the fan noise was a bug in older kernel (before 2.6.35) that does not honor the acpi settings for thinkpads--the new kernel 2.6.35 works like a charm in lucid--the fan is now completely silent, as it should be (Windows 7 settings), and machine runs cool (tempt) all the time. What a pleasure. Now thinking of using Lucid as my full time OS for office work--will be dual booting for Windows related work though.

I thought others could also try this and report here.

get the latest kernel upgrade here: [http://kernel.ubuntu.com/~kernel-ppa/mainline/drm-next/current/](http://kernel.ubuntu.com/~kernel-ppa/mainline/drm-next/current/)

install in this order:

1. Linux-headers ..generic
2. Linux headers
3. linux image

Choose the arch 32-it or 64-bit appropriately though.

Cool,
S:guitar:

Firstly I believe the sequence should be (at least it was for me)
```

1. Linux headers
2. Linux-headers ..generic
3. linux image

```
Secondly: 
My ati graphics driver no longer works as expected. Didn't research it, just googled and saw that the xserver (1.8) used by 1.6.35 isn't supported yet.  My graphics are slow (actually reminds me of the first time I installed ubuntu in 2006, where you first installed the OS w/o the drivers and then compiled them etc.

In short: this kernel upgrade isn't for everyone.

My graphics are slow (actually reminds me of the first time I installed ubuntu in 2006, where you first installed the OS w/o the drivers and then compiled them etc.

In short: this kernel upgrade isn't for everyone.

This is just for the sake of accuracy: in principle, the kernel and xserver versions don't have anything to do. However, it is true that ATi's fglrx does not support X server 1.8. Neither does it support the latest kernels (IIRC, anything newer than 2.6.33 will fail without patches).

---

### Post by Miguel on 2010-07-02

This is a call for help. It turns out that, for a while, ubuntu suspends and awakes fine the first time, but on the next suspend (which looks fine according to /var/log/pm-suspend), it won't wake up. I'm starting to suspect a faulty BIOS (I'm currently on 3.18).

If there are other T400 users here (don't hide! I can see you!), does suspend and resume work reliably for you? If so, could you tell me your BIOS version? You don't need to reboot and enter your BIOS, it should be the last line you see after the command "dmesg | grep BIOS". In my case:

### Post by StickyTape on 2010-09-08
My manager and I decided in 2000 that we would start receiving laptops from IBM, getting a batch of T21s. When the IT bubble hit, and I went to college, I was given the T21(600Mhz, 256MB RAM, 6GB HD) as part of a redundancy package. That T21 once fell down a flight of stairs in a Dutch bar in a laptop bag and was fine..

I used it continually from then up until 2008, at which point it had frequent total freezes, most likely due to hardware failure, as it occurred in Linux, XP, and Windows 2000. The poor old dear.

I am still in an academic environment and really wanted something close to my old T21 and so went for the X61, which has met all my expectations for speed, portability, solidity, and reliability. I specifically chose the fastest dual proc (2.3 Ghz of the later Penryn type) and with all the gadgets save the tablet (alas, beyond my budgetary capacity). It is going solid but the keyboard (Chicony) is wearing after two years of solid use, and I will replace it with an NMB model for library usage.

The X61 will last me long enough until Lenovo come back to their senses and produce 4:3 screens again for their X series. A widescreen on an ultraportable is close to useless for document reading.. In the meantime, I have the last thinkpad business warrior, functionality über alles, solid and handsome, but innocent of time and its changing fashions.

### Post by mini_g on 2010-12-27
**Dezfor**: I'd personally stay away from the ThinkPad Edge if you can possibly afford a "true" ThinkPad.  The Edge is basically a glorified IdeaPad with a TrackPoint and the ThinkPad logo.

For one, it's not made of the same material as the other ThinkPads are.  It uses a lower quality construction for the exterior framing and such.

The Edge has standard ABS plastic.  [_The others do not use nearly such a low-grade material for both the lid and base_](http://forum.thinkpads.com/viewtopic.php?p=570471#p570471).

It's missing the ThinkLight.  This is an addictive MUST if you desire low to no-light situations.

I'd also personally test this in real life before you purchase it, as you might not like it upon having typed on it.

The main thing going for it is that it's the only one with the option of an AMD GPU with a TrackPoint in one package in my opinion.

In leaving, do *not* purchase the x100e if you value the ThinkPad name.  It's _***FAR***_ too weak.  The keyboard's soft, the whole design just doesn't feel the same as other X series models, and is just a weak design overall in my own opinion.  It just feels as though it's going to deal with the motherboard flexing FAR worse than the X32.

---

While I cannot vouche for the validity there is a blog about installing the drivers for the x3100; [[COLOR="Blue"]_How to install Intel GM965 Graphics (X3100 chip; intel video driver) on Ubuntu _[/COLOR]]("http://opensource-openmind.blogspot.com/2007/10/intel-gm965-graphics-x3100-chip-intel.html"). Intel usually are supported, but I would look around and see if anybody has had issues with that video card (chip?).

### Post by Astinsan on 2011-09-18
If you have issues with flash you can also try this
put :
OverrideGPUValidation = 1
in this file :
/etc/adobe/mms.cfg

Lets you use hardware acceleration in unsupported situations.

### Post by dave2001 on 2011-10-04
I have just installed 11.04 on my Thinkpad T60. I see some improvements and some detriments. 

The Good: Better graphics support! The radeon driver is (for the most part) finally providing KMS for my ATI X1400 graphics card without resulting in a Black Screen 0' Death. Except as noted below, great video playback and 3D effect support. I hated Unity, so went back to classic desktop. Installed Compiz CCSM from repos, and a custom built emerald window manager and things are looking pretty snazzy.  It runs fairly cool, CPU rarely reaches above 50C. Because of that whole "Ubuntu is killing my HDD" scare a while back, I checked to make sure there is no excessive hard disk load-cycling going on, and it cycles even less than Windows7 (this is a dual boot machine). 

The Bad:  Flash Video! Anytime a flash video is played in any browser on fullscreen, the audio becomes terribly garbled. I watch a lot of streaming video's, so this is very annoying. I'm quite sure it has to do with the radeon driver. I've tried every type and variation of flash player, browser, and plugin. I've tried various sound fixes. None worked. But booting with "radeon.modeset=0" in the kernel options fixed the issue right away. Of course then all video playback becomes choppy and has screen tearing. Guess I'm going to try and put together an xorg.conf to improve things and go UMS instead of KMS.

---

### Post by dave2001 on 2011-10-04

Have you tried doing a fresh install rather than an upgrade? I'd give that a shot. Natty has some big differences from the older versions, I've heard the upgrade doesn't always work correctly as a result.

### Post by Xianath on 2011-10-24
I got a ThinkPad T410i at work. The SSD had no TRIM and even a year after Samsung had released a firmware that enabled it, Lenovo still had not (and it would not be picked up by Samsung's update utility because Lenovo had rebranded it). What it meant was that write speeds went down to floppy-disk speed (seriously, 150K/sec?!) in about six weeks of usage.

Eventually Lenovo did release a firmware upgrade that, quite frankly, bricked the SSD. What can I say...

I switched to a Ubuntu LiveCD but the optical drive failed in about two weeks of usage. It literally cut its own umbilical. The ribbon cable somehow got pinched when closing the tray door, and now the drive spins but wouldn't read or write anything, and needs a paperclip to get the CD out.

I'm now booting Ubuntu off a USB pendrive, and using a homemade USB->serial converter to connect to agetty on my home server. Its days as an expensive serial terminal are also near an end though, as the USB ports have become so flimsy the pendrive falls out if I lift the machine and don't hold it in. I suppose I could rubber-band it in or something, but this is getting ridiculous. And to think I could have had a MacBook Pro instead!

There was hardly a sturdier machine than the IBM T40s but ThinkPad is not the brand it used to be now that Lenovo makes them. I thought Dells were a c**pshoot but now Lenovo tops my list of brands to avoid like the plague.

---

### Post by dave2001 on 2011-10-24
I've also been less than impressed with lenovo support. The official lenovo Windows software and drivers for my T60 were buggy in every version (assuming they worked at all). 
Also, comparing the build quality of the Lenovo T60 with the older IBM A20m... the newer lenovo machine was showing more wear after a year than the decade old A20m.
I love the layout of thinkpads.. the trackpoint is something I'd really like to see more laptop makers providing, and I also really appreciate a "centered" keyboard.. which also seems less common in the new machines I've been looking at recently. 
So are there any good alternatives to a thinkpad out there? Or is the quality and support of ALL products degrading?

### Post by MikeDK on 2011-10-25
Am I the only one with T500 with intel x4500HD chip, that has issues with metacity been blanked out once in a while, hope it's the same bug as back in hardy or ibex, using Natty x86_64 on classic desktop, 

here's my xorg.conf

```
Section "Monitor"
        Identifier      "Configured Monitor"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
        Identifier      "Default Screen"
        Monitor         "Configured Monitor"
        Device          "Configured Video Device"
        DefaultDepth    24
EndSection

Section "Device"
        Identifier      "Intel GMA x4500HD"
        Driver      "intel"
	BusID	"PCI:0:2:0"
# For better OpenGL performance
	Option		"FramebufferCompression"	"TRUE"
EndSection

Section "DRI"
	Mode 0666
EndSection
```

I'm using FrameBufferCompression because it makes text on certain sites in firefox look better and not all smeared out and blurry.

hope some of you have some better solutions for this.

Btw, actually have good acceleration in 3d, good performance in tuxracer(extremetuxracer) with Terrain details set to 100% instead of the standard 75%.

Kind regards mikedk

### Post by Miguel on 2012-01-14
Heh, I've grown to appreciate my T400 more lately. It's no coincidence that happened after my employer bought me a Dell Latitude E6220. Okay, yeah, the Dell has a top of the line i7 processor and an SSD, so it's blazing fast. Plus it's ubuntu certified, so ACPI works like a charm. After "whispering" a few kernel modifiers plus powertop I get about 6.4 hours with wireless on. But... [list]
[*] The thinkpad has a much nicer keyboard (layout, plus tact, plus key travel)
[*] I miss the nipple^W I mean the ultranav trackpoint
[*] The trackpad in the thinkpad is not rough in the scrolling edge (this on a £1200 machine is a crime)
[*] The screen resolution is **much** better (never ever get a 1366x768 screen if you can avoid it)
[*] The size/weight ratio is better in the thinkpad
[*] I can still get 5 hours with wifi in the thinkpad... after three years. The Dell battery has already lost 2 Wh after a month.
[/list]

Yeah, I'm very disappointed with my new laptop. While I admit I wanted the X220, which was not an option because it wasn't an Apple or a Dell, some of the flaws of the new laptop are just apparent. The only good thing about the Dell is the 50% discount we got.

### Post by mrz80 on 2012-02-06
A few months ago I was compelled by my employer to discontinue use of my beloved T61, because it was out of warranty.  The pc support types wanted to foist the University's "standard" "power user" Dell config on me but I balked.  Then a REALLY sweet 3-day-only deal on an X220i cropped up, and I pounced.  Aside from occasionally missing the palatial screen real estate of the T61, I LOVE this little critter.  11.04's had some recurring wifi issues, and it looks like the SD slot doesn't work (it ate a card full of (fortuntately backed up elsewhere) photos), but those are the only complaints I've got.  Screen's gorgeous, keyboard is great, battery life with the extended pack ranges from plenty long to absurdly long, depending on what I'm working on.  I'd recently gotten a shiny new ASUS Android tablet, but now I find I hardly ever need to use it.  The X220i's just about the perfect blend of portability and functionality.  Oh, and a couple of incidental "drop tests" (one involving a carpeted floor, one involving a rather painful landing on my foot) show that it's properly ThinkPad durable. :)

### Post by dave2001 on 2012-03-01
In my experience the old IBM Thinkpads were built like tanks, and could take just about as much abuse. The Lenovo Thinkpads are lighter, but a lot flimsier. After a year or two, the plastic parts start to crack and chip, the screen hinges get a bit wobbly, etc. 

I'm not sure about the newer ones from the last year or two, as I haven't used one.

### Post by Michael Longval on 2012-08-24
A note to the owners of "old clunkers".

Just wanted to share my experience.  I have an old clunker that I like a lot.  It's a IBM/Lenovo T61p with an Intel Core 2 Duo T9300 2.5Ghz CPU, NVidia graphics card, 4GB ram, a nice 1680x1050 display, wifi, bluetooth, DVD ... all the trappings.  It's even got a fingerprint reader (which I don't use because it's less secure than a good password).

I bought it in a used computer store a little more than a year ago.  By my estimate I paid less than a sixth the initial retail price of roughly $2500.00 

Ok it's kinda bulky and heavy by today's standard of the ultra-thin MacBook Air my son uses, but I like it because I'm not worried that I'm going to break the darn thing when I handle it.

I installed Ubuntu (12.04 recently) and it works like a charm.  Everything works OOTB (out of the box) ... except the fingerprint scanner, you have to install another package... but that is a niggle.

The battery is old, but I was still getting a little less than 2 hours on a charge, which I consider not bad for a now 5 year old laptop.

So here I was with my old clunker happily chugging along, when I decided to go a little crazy.

I intalled a OCZ 120 GB SSD.  Now I know what most are thinking... why waste an SSD on a 5 year old laptop?  Well I can answer that with this:  SPEED and BATTERY LIFE.

The difference in boot times, and load times is ASTOUNDING.  The extension to the battery life is about 25% to 30%.  Now please understand that this is all subjective.  I did however measure some boot times:  Power button to login: less than 30 seconds.  Full desktop in less than another 15 seconds (INCLUDING the time to type in my password).

So that is my story.  So for those of you who are still chugging away on old hardware and wondering if you can get more life out of it, maybe this will inspire you.

PS:  To get the full potential out of the T61p with an SSD, I had to reflash the BIOS with a third party BIOS called "MIDDLETON" (as per the name of the guy who did the modifications) to allow the T61p SATA bus to operate at SATA2 speeds (300Mbps) as opposed to it's original SATA 1 speeds of 150Mbps.  The reasons for the initial limitations are technical, but the laptop chipset was designed to operate at SATA2 speeds, so it's not like I am "overclocking" the SATA bus.

Here is the link to the "MIDDLETON" BIOS (which btw works on other Thinkpad models).  (note: I have NO affiliation with "MIDDLETON" although his BIOS mod works great.)

[http://forum.notebookreview.com/lenovo-ibm/459591-t61-x61-sata-ii-1-5-gb-s-cap-willing-pay-solution-8.html]("http://forum.notebookreview.com/lenovo-ibm/459591-t61-x61-sata-ii-1-5-gb-s-cap-willing-pay-solution-8.html")

Happy hacking ;) 

Mike

### Post by Ansible on 2012-09-02
I had a T61P for 3 or 4 years, and it worked very well for me.  One morning it wouldn't boot, just beeped.  The beep code indicated mobo failure or video failure.  

Now I have the w520, which for the most part is a fine machine. 

I've had pretty good luck with the thinkpad t61p and currently the w520. There are a number of fiddly issues with the w520 but none that impact linux compatability.  Well, except for optimus.

The good:

[LIST]
[*]side fan instead of bottom fan, so ventilation on a bed or other soft surface.

[*]    almost everything just works in linux, drivers all around. see 'the bad' though, about optimus.

[*]    touchpad and trackpoint (the red thing) for mouse control.

[*]    keyboard is pretty good.

[*]    high res monitor.

[*]    quad cores, fast video.

[*]    physically pretty solid and durable.
[/LIST]
The bad:

[LIST]
[*]giant brick of a power supply.

[*]    CD drive constantly opens by accident.

[*]    wifi not as reliable as I'd like. (ed: I got the cheap by-default wifi, there are upgrades I think)

[*]    'optimus' automatically switches between high power and low power video chipsets - on windows. on linux you have to change a setting in the bios, so reboot required.  

[*]    fast usb ports don't work until you've booted into an OS (is that normal for these?)

[*]    cheezy 1394 port, crappy ricoh chipset. Had to buy a card with TI chipset for 1394 cameras that I use for work.
[/LIST]

### Post by samfatboy on 2012-11-28
I have a T61 with the T7300 Core Duo at 2.0 ghz and 2 GB of memory running Ubuntu 11.10 (Onceric) with GNOME 3.2.1, and dual booting with Windows 8 (upgraded from XP)

I got the bright idea of getting the ultra drive bay for an additional HDD, and upgtading my boot and system drive to an SDD. This worked well, except that I also decided to upgrade to 12.04 (Precise) and also trying Unity.  The first thing I noticed was that my system froze in 12.04 -- a lot. I did a lot of research and installed the 3.5 kernel release, which stopped the freezing.  But then I found that the system ran very hot -- Cores at close to 100 celsius whenever using Firefox, Thunderbird, and Libra Office at the same time.  So I installed Thinkfan and made some adjustments.  Still running hot.  

After all of this aggravation, and reading angry posts by many users with similar issues, I decided to re-load 11.10.  All problems now are gone -- and my boot from shut down to full ready desktop is now under 1 minute, no freezing, and core temps around 60 to 70 degrees celsius.

I think I will wait until some of the bugs get resolved in 12.04. I will stay with 11.10 as long as possible -- it is frustrating to know that this solid OS will be unsupported in April - even though I can use the .old repositories.  I am hoping that they make 12.04 more friendly to older laptops.  

By the way, I was very impressed with Windows 8 -- it runs perfect Out Of Box with my T61, is fast, cool, and the boot time is similar to Ubuntu.  But I will remain an Ubuntu die hard as long as they support my hardware.

### Post by topazhn on 2013-01-23
This is my first Lenovo product: T400 purchased on ebay. It was OEM refurbed and seller installed Win7 for refurbed 'puters.

Now I have no prob with Win7; use it on my home rolled desktop - dual boot with Ubuntu 11.1. But for the Thinkpad I decided to go with 12.04. Every thing worked fine - for a while.

The attraction of a lap for me is being able to leave the apps open, suspend operation and safely carry the lap somewhere. Well my new toy stopped suspending.

Love GNU/Linux and the inherited Unix concept of making all visible to them what's prepared to look and learn. 

Went to the system log. Something TPM(?) sending error code 28. Goggle it down. TPM = Trusted Platform Module. Some interesting reading-Wikipedia and such but that's another story. Debated whether anything Ubuntu would be using this thing. Prolly not, so into the BIOS, located the "security chip" entry, made it "invisible". Problem solved.

The T400. Superb. Industrial strength construction. Lots of connectivity and stunning options like being able to slip out the DVD unit and replace it with an extra HDD or other subsystem.

I will definitly buy additional Lenovo products. Love this lap.

---

### Post by topazhn on 2013-01-23
Your problem, like mine, is probably the TPM (Trusted Platform Module). This device is most likely not used by Ubuntu software and can be made "invisible" in the BIOS. My unit is T400 running Ubuntu 12.04. This solved the prob for me and have noticed no unwanted side effects.

---

### Post by hellion0 on 2013-02-27
I'm back in the game! Bought myself a gently used Thinkpad T61 a week ago, and it just arrived today. I swapped out the drives and the Lubuntu install I had on the Latitude fit right in with only one tweak needed - swapping to a PAE-enabled kernel so the 32-bit install could address all 4GB of RAM the machine came with. 

The sole flaw in the hardware is that the left mouse button for the trackpad does not work, but fortunately, the one for the stick *does* work. Just as well, I'm more comfortable on the stick than the trackpad.

Could not be happier right now!
